A ‘W’ does not affect the student’s GPA. • Grade Point Average (GPA): GPA is calculated by dividing [the sum of (grade points earned * credit hours earned) for each course] by [the total attempted credits for GPA]. All courses for which a P/NP, I, W, or RP grade is awarded are excluded from the GPA calculation. • Grade Reports (Transcript): At the end of each term, grade reports are available for viewing on the Fulbright One Stop portal, named Unofficial Transcript. ### Question 62: Why and how am I getting academic suspension?  
### Answer: 

You are getting academic suspension because you have failed to fulfill all the requirements of your Learning Contract while on Academic Probation. The Academic Suspension is entered on your transcript as part of your academic record. You must meet with the Dean's Office, who will establish the conditions that you must meet prior to returning to Fulbright. While on suspension, you may not visit the Fulbright campus unless permission is given from the Dean's Office or the Vice President of Student Affairs for the purpose of attending relevant meetings. Suspensions typically are for one term or one academic year. A student may be suspended a maximum of two times. If you are suspended a third time, your enrolment in the program will be canceled, and you will have to apply for re-admission. You must include with your application for re-admission a letter that addresses the reasons for your suspensions and cancellation, and the measures you have taken to address those reasons. The re-admission decision is made by the Dean's Office in consultation with the appropriate members of faculty and staff. Students who are re-admitted must also re-apply for financial aid.  

<details>  
<summary>References</summary>  

[Source: Academic-Policy_V5.1.pdf, Page: 11]
situation. The Registrar's Office will be informed as a matter of record and follow-up. Three official warnings shall result in Disciplinary Action, constituting Academic Probation or Academic Suspension. 6.3 Academic Probation This is the second level of intervention. It is intended to make students aware that their academic performance puts them at risk of losing the opportunity to study at Fulbright, either temporarily (Suspension) or permanently (Dismissal). Students on Academic Warning who fail to meet all the requirements of their Learning Contract may require an additional Academic Progress Meeting and may be placed on Academic Probation, typically resulting in an updated Learning Contract. Academic Probation typically lasts for a term. 6.4 Academic Suspension A student on Academic Probation who fails to fulfill all the requirements of their Learning Contract may be placed on Academic Suspension. Suspensions are entered on the student’s transcript as part of their academic record. The suspended

[Source: Academic-Policy_V5.1.pdf, Page: 11]
as specified. 6.2 Academic Warning This is usually the first level of intervention for students who are not making satisfactory progress toward their degree and/or who fall below a 2.0 GPA, or for other reasons such as failure of attendance, participation, citizenship, or academic integrity. An Academic Warning is sent out by the Registrar’s Office. The student is required to attend an Academic Progress Meeting during which a Learning Contract will be created with specific conditions tailored to the individual situation. The Registrar's Office will be informed as a matter of record and follow-up. Three official warnings shall result in Disciplinary Action, constituting Academic Probation or Academic Suspension. 6.3 Academic Probation This is the second level of intervention. student must meet with the Dean’s Office, who establishes the conditions that the student must meet prior to returning to Fulbright. While on suspension, a student may not visit the Fulbright campus unless permission is given from the Dean’s Office or the Vice President of Student Affairs for the purpose of attending relevant meetings. Suspensions typically are for one term or one academic year. A student may be suspended a maximum of two times. A student will not be suspended a third time but will instead have their enrolment in the program canceled. A student in this situation must apply for re-admission. The student must include with his or her application for re-admission a letter that addresses the reasons for their suspensions and cancellation, and the measures they have taken to address those reasons. The re-admission decision is made by the Dean’s Office in consultation with the appropriate members of faculty and staff. Students who are re-admitted must also re- apply for financial aid.

### Question 63: How does the P/NP grade work?  
### Answer: 

At Fulbright University Vietnam, students can elect to take a total of 8 credits (typically 2 courses, 4 credits each) in one academic year on a Pass/No Pass basis. This is done by completing a Petition to Elect Pass/No Pass Grade form and submitting it to the Registrar’s Office before 4:00 PM on Friday Week 4 of the term. A grade of ‘C-’ or higher will be counted as a Pass. Courses graded with a Pass grade can be used to meet prerequisite requirements for next-level courses. Any grade below a ‘C-’ will be counted as a No Pass. No credit is granted for this result. The NP grade will be shown on the Official Transcript. Courses with a NP grade cannot be used to meet prerequisite requirements for next-level courses. Once a student converts a course grade option to Pass/No Pass, the grade option cannot be changed back. Pass/No Pass grades do not apply to core courses and cannot be used to count toward major/minor requirements.

### Question 64: How many courses can I take as P/NP at maximum and how will it contribute to the official transcript GPA?  
### Answer: 

You can take a maximum of 2 courses, 4 credits each, on a Pass/No Pass basis in one academic year. However, Pass/No Pass grades do not apply to core courses and cannot be used to count toward major/minor requirements. A grade of 'C-' or higher will be counted as a Pass and can be used to meet prerequisite requirements for next-level courses. Any grade below a 'C-' will be counted as a No Pass, and no credit is granted for this result. The NP grade will be shown on the Official Transcript. Courses with a NP grade cannot be used to meet prerequisite requirements for next-level courses. The Pass/No Pass grades are not included in the GPA calculation.

### Question 65: I've failed the GWP due to personal reasons so will it count toward the 144 maximum credits I can have?  
### Answer: 

Yes, the failed grade for GWP will count toward the total attempted credits, which is part of the 144 maximum credits a student can have. However, if you choose to retake the course, the lower grade will be overwritten by the notation "RP", meaning "repeated", and the higher grade will be used in the GPA calculation. The repeated course credits are counted toward the total attempted credits but not the total earned credits.

In order to make standard progress toward completing the degree, students are required to register for no fewer than 12 credit hours and no more than 20 credit hours per term. ### Question 66: What and how do I get an Academic Warning?  
### Answer: 

An Academic Warning is usually the first level of intervention for students who are not making satisfactory progress toward their degree and/or who fall below a 2.0 GPA, or for other reasons such as failure of attendance, participation, citizenship, or academic integrity. To receive an Academic Warning, a student is required to attend an Academic Progress Meeting during which a Learning Contract will be created with specific conditions tailored to the individual situation. The Registrar's Office will be informed as a matter of record and follow-up.  

<details>  
<summary>References</summary>  

[Source: Academic-Policy_V5.1.pdf, Page: 11]
as specified. 6.2 Academic Warning This is usually the first level of intervention for students who are not making satisfactory progress toward their degree and/or who fall below a 2.0 GPA, or for other reasons such as failure of attendance, participation, citizenship, or academic integrity. An Academic Warning is sent out by the Registrar’s Office. The student is required to attend an Academic Progress Meeting during which a Learning Contract will be created with specific conditions tailored to the individual situation. The Registrar's Office will be informed as a matter of record and follow-up. Three official warnings shall result in Disciplinary Action, constituting Academic Probation or Academic Suspension. 6.3 Academic Probation This is the second level of intervention. It is intended to make students aware that their academic performance puts them at risk of losing the opportunity to study at Fulbright, either temporarily (Suspension) or permanently (Dismissal). Academic Probation typically lasts for a term. 6.4 Academic Suspension A student on Academic Probation who fails to fulfill all the requirements of their Learning Contract may be placed on Academic Suspension. ### Question 68: Can you provide me with some courses suggestion to take to major in Math?  
### Answer: 

To major in Applied Mathematics, you would need to take a combination of foundation, intermediate, advanced, and applied courses. Here are some examples:

Foundation Courses:
- Linear Algebra
- Single variable Calculus
- Introduction to Statistics
- Multivariable Calculus

Intermediate Courses:
- Probability
- Differential Equations
- Discrete Mathematics
- Numerical Analysis

Advanced Courses:
- Advanced Statistics
- Statistical Learning
- Stochastic Calculus
- Optimization
- Partial Differential Equations

Elective Applied Courses (at least 2, at least one at 200 level):
- Game theory (Economics)
- The Economics of Corruption (Economics)
- Money and Banking (Economics)
- Signal, Systems, and Control (Engineering)
- Computer Vision (Engineering)
- Introduction to Machine Learning (Computer Science)
- Algorithm (Computer Science)
- Operations Research (Applied Mathematics)
- Introduction to Quantitative Finance (Applied Mathematics)

Pure Mathematics Course (at least 1):
- Abstract Algebra
- Real Analysis

Research seminars (optional)

Capstone project (optional)

Please note that you may not double count a course for two different requirements. For example, Operations research can only count for either 1 Advanced course or 1 Elective course, but not both. Also, consultation with an academic advisor is required for course selection.  

<details>  
<summary>References</summary>  

[Source: Major Descriptions and Flowcharts_OfficialVersion.pdf, Page: 17]
of areas with applications in Mathematics: • Applied Statistics (Economics, Social Sciences, Mathematical Finance, Bioinformatics…) • Engineering Mathematics (Signal processing, Numerical simulation, Inverse problems…) • Data Science (Machine learning, Artificial intelligence …) Students will take at least 2 advanced courses. Consultation with an academic advisor is required for course selection. Sample Advanced Courses • Advanced Statistics • Statistical Learning • Stochastic Calculus • Numerical Analysis • Optimization • Partial Differential Equations Elective Applied courses: These are the courses from other majors that emphasize the applications of Mathematics.  Students will have to take at least 2 applied courses (at least one at 200 level). If there is any prerequisite, students need to either complete the course’s prerequisites or obtain the instructor’s approval. ### Question 69: How to declare a major in Computer Science?  
### Answer: 

To formally declare Computer Science as their major, a student must complete at least two Computer Science courses. This includes MATH 202 - Discrete Math (4 credits) and either CS 101: Introduction to Programming, CS 103: Programming for Data Science and Visualization, or CS 104: Introduction to Computer Science. After completing these courses, the student must also complete a total of 56 credits in major requirements, which include courses such as CS 201: Data Structures & Algorithms, CS 302: Algorithms & Theory of Computing, and various advanced courses. The exact number and specific courses may vary based on the school's policy.

### Question 70: I'm currently under a General Work Program for Experiential Learning but the company do not pay me in any form. How can I get the subsidy from Fulbright University?  
### Answer: 

The Fulbright University's Experiential Learning Program (ELP) does not provide subsidies for unpaid work experiences. However, if the work experience is part of an academic course, you may be able to receive academic credit for it upon advisor approval. If the work experience is not part of an academic course, you would not be eligible for academic credit or subsidies. It is recommended to consult with your academic advisor for guidance on this matter.

Fulbright’s Experiential Learning Program (ELP) exists to create, standardize, and facilitate academic credit-bearing experiential learning experiences. All full-time, undergraduate, degree- seeking students must complete at least 04 credits and a maximum of 12 credits under the ELP as a graduation requirement. Current ELP streams are housed within Academic Affairs (AA), Career Services (CS), and Center for Entrepreneurship and Innovation (CEI), where each team is responsible for administrative and academic duties of their respective stream(s). The ELP operates within Fulbright’s undergraduate program’s standard operating procedures and is developed in consultation with undergraduate program leadership and faculty. ### Question 71: Can you give me the process of making a Capstone for graduation?  
### Answer: 

The Capstone process for graduation in the context provided involves the following steps:

1. Capstone I: In this semester, you actively conduct research and refine your project proposal and plan. You focus on gathering and organizing your information or other materials needed to realize your project. You meet with your advisor regularly and submit midterm and end-of-term submissions as per the schedule.

2. Capstone II: In this semester, you focus more on production, whether it is writing or realizing an applied project. You participate in research in support of your final submission. You submit midterm submissions (drafts of chapters, documentation of an applied project’s progress, a rough draft or outline of a thesis) and an end-of-term submission (a completed written thesis and a finished project).

3. Capstone Presentation: At the end of Capstone II, you are highly recommended to present your findings to the larger Fulbright community. The presentation format can be decided between you and your advisors and can be a powerpoint presentation, a board presentation, or a combination of both. The presentation usually takes place at the end of Capstone II, during the last two weeks of the semester.

4. Capstone Grading: The Capstone project is graded through assessment of the final submission in Capstone II. The research process is evaluated by the thesis advisor only. The grading rubric for Capstone projects includes the Research Process, Project Proposal, Literature Review, Production, and Presentation.

5. Capstone for Graduation with Distinction: If you wish to graduate with distinction, you may want to complete the Capstone year. The Capstone sequence begins in the Fall with Capstone I and ends in the Spring with Capstone II, culminating with a formal defense and a final evaluation by two readers.

### Answer: 

To graduate with Honors, a student's capstone project must be graded Honors. The GPA is not directly mentioned as a requirement for a distinctive graduation in the given context. However, it's worth noting that the GPA is a significant factor in determining a student's academic standing and eligibility for various opportunities, but it's not explicitly stated as a requirement for a distinctive graduation.

### Question 73: How can I graduate with Honor or lie within the top GPA?  
### Answer: 

To graduate with honors in the Social Studies major, you need to complete the Capstone I and Capstone II, and your Capstone must be graded as Honors pass. For the Computer Science major, you need to maintain a GPA of 3.5 throughout your senior year. For the Social Studies minor, you need to complete Social Inquiry and at least one course in the Social Studies Program. For the Social Studies major, you need to complete Social Inquiry, and at least two courses at the 100 or 200 level. The GPA requirements for the Social Studies major capstone are 3.6. It is important to note that you should discuss your proposals with program coordinators and potential advisors to prepare your applications. Successful capstone applicants must maintain the required GPA throughout their senior year to be able to earn an Honors for the capstone. Failure to maintain the required GPA will result in the capstone being capped at Pass.

### Question 74: How many courses can I take with P/NP grade in total?  
### Answer: 

You can take a total of 8 credits (typically 2 courses, 4 credits each) in one academic year on a Pass/No Pass basis.

Question: What is the minimum grade to earn credit for a course?
Answer: A grade of 'D' is the minimum grade to earn credit for a course.

Question: What is the minimum grade to pass a course taken on Pass/No Pass basis, or to be counted toward major/minor requirements, or to be used to fulfill a prerequisite to register for more advanced courses?
Answer: A minimum grade of 'C-' is required to pass a course taken on Pass/No Pass basis, or to be counted toward major/minor requirements, or to be used to fulfill a prerequisite to register for more advanced courses.

Question: Can I change back a course grade option from Pass/No Pass to a letter grade?
Answer: Once a student converts a course grade option to Pass/No Pass, the grade option cannot be changed back.

Question: Can Pass/No Pass grades be used to count toward major/minor requirements?
Answer: No, Pass/No Pass grades cannot be used to count toward major/minor requirements.

Question: Can I use a Pass grade to meet prerequisite requirements for next-level courses?
Answer: Yes, courses graded with a Pass grade can be used to meet prerequisite requirements for next-level courses.

Question: What happens if I receive a grade below a 'C-' in a course taken on Pass/No Pass basis?
Answer: Any grade below a 'C-' will be counted as a No Pass. No credit is granted for this result. The NP grade will be shown on the Official Transcript. Courses with a NP grade cannot be used to meet prerequisite requirements for next-level courses.

Question: What is the maximum number of courses I can repeat if I have received a grade of 'D+', 'D', 'F', or NP for a course?
Answer: Students may repeat a course if they have received a grade of 'D+', 'D', 'F', or NP for the course or have withdrawn and received a grade of 'W'. There is no specified limit on the number of times a course can be repeated.

Question: What happens if I am unable to complete the work in a course because of illness, family emergency, or other exceptional circumstances?
Answer: If a student is unable to complete the work in a course because of illness, family emergency, or other exceptional circumstances, a temporary grade of ‘I’ (Incomplete) may be awarded by the faculty until unfinished course requirements are completed. The student has until the date agreed upon with the faculty (not to exceed 6 months from the end of the course) to complete all remaining course work; otherwise, the student will be given an F grade.

Question: How is the GPA calculated?
Answer: The GPA is calculated by dividing [the sum of (grade points earned * credit hours earned) for each course] by [the total attempted credits for GPA]. All courses for which a P/NP, I, W, or RP grade is awarded are excluded from the GPA calculation.

Question: Where can I view my grade reports?
Answer: At the end of each term, grade reports are available for viewing on the Fulbright One Stop portal, named Unofficial Transcript. Paper copies of grade reports, named Transcript of Records, can be issued by the Registrar’s Office upon students’ request.

Question: Can I use a course with a Pass grade to fulfill a prerequisite to register for more advanced courses if it is not a core course?
Answer: Yes, courses graded with a Pass grade can be used to meet prerequisite requirements for next-level courses, as long as they are not core courses.

Question: Can I use a course with a Pass grade to count toward major/minor requirements if it is not a core course?
Answer: No, Pass/No Pass grades cannot be used to count toward major/minor requirements, regardless of whether the course is a core course or not.

Question: Can I use a course with a Pass grade to count toward elective requirements?
Answer: Yes, grades ‘D’ or ‘D+’ can only be counted toward the requirements for elective courses.

Question: Can I use a course with a No Pass grade to meet prerequisite requirements for next-level courses?
Answer: No, courses with a No Pass grade cannot be used to meet prerequisite requirements for next-level courses.  

<details>  
<summary>References</summary>  

[Source: Academic-Policy_V5.1.pdf, Page: 10]
take a total of 8 credits (typically 2 courses, 4 credits each) in one academic year on a Pass/No Pass basis by completing a Petition to Elect Pass/No Pass Grade form and submitting it to the Registrar’s Office before 4:00 PM on Friday Week 4 of the term (16-week term).  The following conditions apply: o Once a student converts a course grade option to Pass/No Pass, the grade option cannot be changed back. o Pass/No Pass grades do not apply to core courses. They cannot be used to count toward major/minor requirements. o The Registrar’s Office is responsible for converting to the P/NP after receiving the final grade submission by the instructor at the end of the term. o A grade of ‘C-’ or higher will be counted as a Pass. Courses graded with a Pass grade can be used to meet prerequisite requirements for next-level courses. o Any grade below a ‘C-’ will be counted as a No Pass. No credit is granted for this result. The NP grade will be shown on the Official Transcript. Courses with a NP grade cannot be used to

Students pursuing a double major must complete all requirements for each major. If two majors (or two minors, or a major and a minor) share cross- listed or tagged1 courses, up to 8 credits (two courses) can be used to satisfy both sets of requirements. This limit is per each pair of majors (or major and minor) and does not restrict the total number of double-counted credits or courses a student can claim. For example, a student can major in both A and B and minor in C with a total of 6 double-counted courses: two in A and B, two in B and C, and two in A and C. ### Question 75: How many types of absences are there?  
### Answer: 

There are at least 8 types of absences. These include general absences, military leave, excused absence due to university-sponsored events/activities, indefinite leaves, administrative leave of absence, and absences due to exceptional circumstances. Additionally, there may be other types of absences not explicitly mentioned in the context.

Fulbright is committed to supporting student learning when absences are unavoidable.

### Question 76: How many types of leave of absence are there and how can I have one?  
### Answer: 

There are three types of leave of absence at Fulbright: Personal Leave, Medical Leave, and Administrative Leave of Absence. To have a leave of absence, a student must complete and submit the Undergraduate Leave of Absence form before the last day of class. For a medical leave, the student must also submit the Fulbright Impact Assessment form and all medical supporting documents. The duration of the leave is determined in conjunction with the health services professional, the Registrar’s Office, and the student. Indefinite leaves are not permitted. For an administrative leave, a student may be placed on leave if they have an outstanding student account balance in an enrolled term without informing Student Financial Services to request a late and/or an extension of tuition fee payment. Before placing a student in this type of absence, the Student Financial Services team will attempt to determine the circumstances and request a timely response from the student.

### Question 79: What is the school's policy on academic dishonesty, and how are violations handled?  
### Answer: 

The school's policy on academic dishonesty, as described in Fulbright University Vietnam's Code of Academic Integrity, states that academic integrity is essential for academic success and personal development. Violations of academic integrity, such as plagiarism, cheating, fabrication, and facilitating academic dishonesty, are taken seriously. The Registrar's Office will be informed as a matter of record and follow-up. Three official warnings shall result in Disciplinary Action, constituting Academic Probation or Academic Suspension. Academic Probation is the second level of intervention, intended to make students aware that their academic performance puts them at risk of losing the opportunity to study at Fulbright, either temporarily (Suspension) or permanently (Dismissal). A student on Academic Probation who fails to fulfill all the requirements of their Learning Contract may be placed on Academic Suspension. Suspensions are entered on the student’s transcript as part of their academic record. The capstone is also subject to these regulations.

### Question 80: What are the policies regarding retaking exams or improving grades?  
### Answer: 

At the university, students are required to repeat core courses if they receive an F grade or if they receive a grade below 'C-' in courses that count towards their major or minor. Students may also repeat a course if they have received a grade of 'D+', 'D', 'F', or 'NP', or have withdrawn and received a 'W'. In special cases, a student may request to repeat a course after receiving a grade higher than a 'D+' following consultation with the academic/major advisor, the course instructor, and the Registrar's Office. The higher grade will be kept and used in the GPA calculation, while the lower grade will be overwritten by the notation "RP" (repeated) and remain on the transcript. Credits of the repeated course are counted toward the total attempted credits. A student may not retake the same course for the third time unless they failed the second time or if a specific grade is needed to meet the major requirements. Students should be aware that repeating courses may affect their eligibility for next-level courses.  

<details>  
<summary>References</summary>  

[Source: Academic-Policy_V5.1.pdf, Page: 10]

Credits of the repeated course are counted toward the total attempted credits. A student may not retake the same course for the third time unless he/she failed the second time or if a specific grade is needed to meet the major requirements. The signed request form must be submitted no later than 4:00 PM to the Registrar’s Office, on the last day of the term end date. • W = Withdrawal: A grade of ‘W’ (Withdrawal) is issued for a student- initiated withdrawal after 4:00 PM Friday Week 4 and prior to the end of Week 8. ### Question 81: How does the university accommodate students with chronic illnesses or personal emergencies that affect attendance?  
### Answer: 

The university accommodates students with chronic illnesses or personal emergencies that affect attendance by considering these circumstances as exceptional. This includes exceptional medical circumstances, close bereavement, victim of a serious crime, disabilities for which reasonable adjustments are not yet in place, exceptional and unforeseeable transport difficulties, legal proceedings, military leave, excused absence due to university-sponsored events/activities, and emergency situations. In these cases, students are expected to submit appropriate documentation and contact their instructors to initiate arrangements to make up any missed work. The university encourages instructors to allow students to make up any missed assignments if the absence is reasonable and to inform the student if they are in danger of failing the course because of class absence or missed assignments. If a student determines that medical leave would be beneficial due to a chronic illness, they must submit the Undergraduate Leave of Absence form and the Fulbright Impact Assessment form, along with all medical supporting documents, before the last day of class. The leave duration is determined in conjunction with the health services professional, the Registrar’s Office, and the student. Indefinite leaves are not permitted.

EXCEPTIONAL CIRCUMSTANCES: The University acknowledges that sometimes a student will experience circumstances that will impact their ability to fulfill the expectations of the University, including but not limited to assessment, attendance, and paying fees. Circumstances that may fall into this category are: • Exceptional medical circumstances, e.g., hospitalization or incapacitation through injury, illness, or mental health crisis. • Close bereavement, e.g., partner, child, parent, sibling, grandparent, and grandchild. Housemates or very close friends may also be considered as ‘close’, though evidence of the relationship may be required. • Victim of a serious crime • Disabilities for which reasonable adjustments are not yet in place and where the delay is not due to the student • Exceptional and unforeseeable transport difficulties e.g., major transport incidents, cancelled flights. This does not include everyday issues, e.g., traffic congestion, missed buses or trains. • Legal proceedings requiring

The university and instructor(s) are encouraged to accommodate the students. • Excused absence due to the university-sponsored events/activities for academic, non-academic, and recognized student organizations (including but not limited to student athletes, student council presidents, student club members representing university, etc.).  If a student must miss class(es) for a university-sponsored event, the faculty or staff responsible for that event requests a University Official Activity Excused Absence Request Form and submit it to the Dean’s Office, keeping Academic Affairs and Registrar’s Office in cc- ed for the record. ### Question 82: Are students allowed to use AI tools like ChatGPT for assignments? If so, under what conditions?  
### Answer: 

Yes, students can use AI tools like ChatGPT for assignments, but they must provide comprehensive documentation covering every aspect of AI usage. This documentation should include the objective and scope of using AI, the tools and platforms employed, the process and methodology of incorporating AI, ethical and copyright issues associated with using AI, and how these concerns will be addressed throughout the project. This comprehensive documentation promotes transparency, offers insight into AI's role in the creative process, and highlights the originality and human contributions to the project. It is important to note that students must obtain IRB approval before the period of their Fulbright-affiliated research, and they are advised to begin their IRB application as soon as their Capstone application is accepted, or during Capstone I at the latest. Failure to do so may result in delays to the project and/or its suspension.

Creative projects that incorporate generative AI must include comprehensive documentation covering every aspect of AI usage. ### Question 83: Where can I get support for mental health treatment?  
### Answer: 

The context does not provide specific information about where to get support for mental health treatment. However, it does mention a Resource Guide for Local Mental Health Services as one of the potential Capstone by Applied Projects. This suggests that such a resource guide may be available and could potentially provide information about local mental health services. Additionally, the Mental Health First Aid Training Program could also provide some information about resources for mental health treatment. It is recommended to consult with a primary or secondary advisor from the Psychology program or a non-academic advisor (e.g., a mental health practitioner) for more specific information.

### Question 85: Where can I find resources to facilitate my graduate program after Fulbright undergraduate?  
### Answer: 

For resources to facilitate your graduate program after Fulbright undergraduate, you may refer to the Experiential Learning Program (ELP) at Fulbright University Vietnam. The ELP is housed within Academic Affairs (AA), Career Services (CS), and Center for Entrepreneurship and Innovation (CEI), where each team is responsible for administrative and academic duties of their respective stream(s). The ELP operates within Fulbright’s undergraduate program’s standard operating procedures and is developed in consultation with undergraduate program leadership and faculty. You can find more details about the ELP on the Fulbright University Vietnam OneStop website.  

<details>  
<summary>References</summary>

RE-ADMISSION TO FULL-TIME STATUS: Students who wish to return to Fulbright after withdrawing formally or without permission must reapply for admission and financial aid. Students who are readmitted must follow the academic regulations, degree program, and curriculum requirements in effect at the time of readmission. The academic record of the student remains unchanged upon reinstatement except under special circumstances decided by the Dean’s Office.

Fulbright’s Experiential Learning Program (ELP) exists to create, standardize, and facilitate academic credit-bearing experiential learning experiences. All full-time, undergraduate, degree- seeking students must complete at least 04 credits and a maximum of 12 credits under the ELP as a graduation requirement. Current ELP streams are housed within Academic Affairs (AA), Career Services (CS), and Center for Entrepreneurship and Innovation (CEI), where each team is responsible for administrative and academic duties of their respective stream(s). The ELP operates within Fulbright’s undergraduate program’s standard operating procedures and is developed in consultation with undergraduate program leadership and faculty. ### Question 87: Where can I get the assist for internship?  
### Answer: 

Industry mentors may be available for project guidance, helping bridge academic learning and industry practice. They could be secondary advisors for Capstone projects, but not primary advisors or independent reviewers. They could also be invited to join the capstone panel. As either a secondary advisor or a member of the capstone panel, industry mentors could participate in grading. However, it is not specified that they can assist with internships. You should consult with your advisors or the IS faculty for internship opportunities.

FUV has a student research fund which supports student’s research projects, including capstone. • If there is no viable ways to get access to the equipment, changes to the experimetnal design might be necessary. Students should discuss with their advisors. Obtaining all these resources (funding, equipment, samples…etc) might necessitates singficant paperwork.

### Question 88: How can I get the information of campus usage for events so that I can have proper place to study without getting interrupted?  
### Answer: 

To get the information of campus usage for events, you should contact the university's event management office or the student activities office. They can provide you with a schedule of upcoming events and help you find suitable study spaces that are not being used for events during the times you need to study. Additionally, you can check the university's website or mobile app for event listings and campus maps to find available study spaces.

### Question 89: I used to take an undergraduate program at another university and I want to transfer credit of studied courses at that university. What should I do?  
### Answer: 

To transfer credit of studied courses at another university to your Fulbright undergraduate degree, you should submit an Application for Credit Transfer, along with the required information on the course(s), to the Office of the Registrar. The Registrar will coordinate with the Office of the Dean to determine whether credit is justified. A maximum of 64 credit hours can be transferred and credited to a Fulbright undergraduate degree. You should provide information about the course(s) for which you are applying to transfer, including course curriculum, learning outcomes, course content, and assessments. For more information, please refer to the Transfer Credit policy_Final_V3.0 published in the One Stop portal.  

<details>  
<summary>References</summary>  

[Source: Academic-Policy_V5.1.pdf, Page: 10]
courses delivered by Fulbright. When applying for Credit Transfer, a student is responsible for providing all the information that is requested about the course(s) for which they are applying to transfer. Information may include but not limited to course curriculum, learning outcomes, course content, and assessments. To apply for Credit Transfer or an Exemption, students should submit an Application for Credit Transfer, along with the required information on the course(s), to the Office of the Registrar. The Registrar will coordinate with the Office of the Dean to determine whether credit or an exemption is justified. Credit Transfer from A-level, Advanced Placement (AP), International Baccalaureate (IB), and Cambridge International Exam (CIE) courses will be determined according to the AP/IB/CIE Credit Policy (in development). For more information, please refer to the Transfer Credit policy_Final_V3.0 published in the One Stop portal.

### Question 90: What are the policies of CWP?  
### Answer: 

The policies of the Capstone Writing Project (CWP) at Fulbright University Vietnam (Fulbright) include the following:

1. The capstone project must be approved by the major coordinator and the Dean’s Office if there is an exception to the university-wide policy.

2. Applications for the capstone project should demonstrate awareness of the scope and practicalities needed to realize the project. Projects without current faculty expertise may not be approved.

3. Successful capstone applicants must maintain a 3.6 GPA throughout their senior year to earn an Honors for the capstone. Failure to maintain the required GPA will result in the capstone being capped at Pass.

4. If the applied project requires logistical arrangements outside the university’s typical academic scope, the student must notify the Psychology faculty and relevant Fulbright University functionaries well in advance. This includes events organized by the student in partnership with groups inside or outside Fulbright University Vietnam, applied projects taking place on the FUV campus, and any project that may raise liability concerns for the student or the institution.

5. The planning and production of the creative project is properly aligned with the agreed-upon capstone schedule, and documentation of the process of creating the text(s) is comprehensive.

6. The concept of the capstone project should develop a compelling central idea, opinion, message, and/or story, demonstrating evidence of original, creative, and/or innovative thinking. The concept should draw upon connections between literary and theoretical works and/or the society and world around them.

7. The aesthetic decisions, methods, and process pertinent to the work should be discussed in connection with current conversations in the chosen genre. The design of the manuscript and rationale for its organization should be described, with reference to any literary models, if applicable. Key terms, theories, texts, techniques, writers, and/or movements that are important to the understanding of the work should be referenced.

8. The evaluation criteria for Social Studies capstone proposals include the concept, logistical support, process and documentation, and section scores for concept and process and documentation.

### Question 91: I'm a student athlete then how can I bypass all of physical education courses required to graduate?  
### Answer: 

As a student athlete, you may be able to bypass some of the physical education courses required to graduate, but not all of them. According to the provided context, physical education courses can be double-counted with other courses, but the number of double-counted credits is often limited. If your athletic activities are cross-listed with a physical education course, you might be able to use that course to fulfill the physical education requirement. However, triple counting is not allowed, and any particular course can only be used to satisfy at most two requirements. It's recommended to consult with your academic advisor or the Dean's Office for specific guidance on your situation.  

<details>  
<summary>References</summary>  

[Source: Academic-Policy_V5.1.pdf, Page: 20]
• Physical Education • Political courses These courses do not count toward the 128-credit requirement. All students for whom English is not their first language must take an English Assessment Test required by NECHE Accreditation. 13.8  Double Counting In satisfying degree requirements, some courses can be double-counted. For example, an exploratory course can also be counted as a major course for the corresponding major. However, the number of double-counted credits is often limited (e.g., see subsections 13.2 and 13.3). Additionally, any particular course can only be used to satisfy at most two requirements. For instance, if course X is cross-listed between major A and major B and tagged by minor C, then X can be used to fulfill the requirements of major A and major B, or major A and minor C, or major B and minor C. Triple counting is not allowed. 13.9  Maximal Length of Study Fulbright follows MOET regulations, which state that the maximum time to complete the program cannot exceed double the standard

### Question 92: I'm currently a third year student and moved out of university dormitory after first year but now I'm struggling to find a new accommodation so can I register again for dormitory and will I still have the financial support?  
### Answer: 

If you are experiencing exceptional circumstances such as difficulty finding accommodation, you may be eligible for a Leave of Absence (LOA). During the LOA, you will still be enrolled in the Fulbright undergraduate program, but you will not be registered for any courses. However, you will not be able to participate in other official University activities. If you are granted a LOA, you may be able to return to the university dormitory in the future. Regarding financial support, it is not clear from the provided context whether your financial aid will be affected during the LOA. It is recommended to contact the Student Financial Services team to discuss your specific situation and potential solutions.  

<details>  
<summary>References</summary>  

[Source: Academic-Policy_V5.1.pdf, Page: 15]
Student Financial Services to request a late and/or an extension of tuition fee payment. Before placing a student in this type of absence, the Student Financial Services team will attempt to determine the circumstances and request a timely response from the student. With this absence status, students are unable to register for new course(s) during the registration period, participate in classes or a Work-Study Program in the current term. A student will only be reinstated as “Active” status if the outstanding balance is clear. If the student anticipates being unable to clear the account on time, the student should meet with the Student Financial Services team as soon as possible to request assistance and alternative solutions. After the approved period of absence, a student is put on Administrative Leave of Absence (Admin LOA) for a maximum of one term if the Registrar’s Office receives no response of return confirmation or no registration in the returning term. ### Question 94: How many ways are there provided by the university can I get the support in my academic path?  
### Answer: 

The university provides support in several ways. Firstly, students have access to labs, tools, and software relevant to their project work. Support will be provided for learning new software or techniques where necessary. Mentorship is also available from industry mentors for project guidance, helping bridge academic learning and industry practice. They could be secondary advisors for Capstone projects, but not primary advisors or independent reviewers. They could also be invited to join the capstone panel. As either a secondary advisor or a member of the capstone panel, industry mentors could participate in grading.

Secondly, funding and material procurement will be available for projects. Policies on budgeting and purchasing will be provided.

Thirdly, in exceptional circumstances, the university acknowledges that sometimes a student will experience circumstances that will impact their ability to fulfill the expectations of the University, including but not limited to assessment, attendance, and paying fees. Circumstances that may fall into this category are: exceptional medical circumstances, close bereavement, victim of a serious crime, disabilities for which reasonable adjustments are not yet in place and where the delay is not due to the student, exceptional and unforeseeable transport difficulties, and legal proceedings requiring.

Lastly, if the applied project requires logistical arrangements outside the university’s typical academic scope, the student must notify the Psychology faculty and relevant Fulbright University functionaries well in advance. This includes events organized by the student in partnership with groups inside or outside Fulbright University Vietnam, applied projects taking place on the FUV campus, and any project that may raise liability concerns for the student or the institution.

### Question 95: Can you give me the information about student fees and charges policy?  
### Answer: 

The fees and charges policy for undergraduate students at Fulbright can be found in the "Fees & Charges Guide". If a student experiences exceptional circumstances that impact their ability to fulfill the expectations of the University, tuition credit may be considered. However, no reduction in tuition is granted to students whose course withdrawal results in fewer than 12 academic credits. Students should be aware that course withdrawals may affect their financial aid eligibility if resulting in fewer than the minimum credits for full-time enrollment. If a student anticipates being unable to clear their account on time, they should meet with the Student Financial Services team as soon as possible to request assistance and alternative solutions.

A student will only be reinstated as “Active” status if the outstanding balance is clear. If the student anticipates being unable to clear the account on time, the student should meet with the Student Financial Services team as soon as possible to request assistance and alternative solutions. ### Question 97: I'm having some bad experience with a professor teaching a course. The problem was his way of delivering does not meet academic standard and I want to say something about this with people having higher authorities. What should I do?  
### Answer: 

If you believe there has been an error in the way a course is being taught, you can first discuss the matter with the course instructor(s). If the issue remains unresolved, you may file an appeal. To do this, you should submit the Review of Final Grade Request form to the Registrar's Office within five (05) business days from the date on which the Registrar's Office posts the final grade for the term. The Registrar's Office will then inform the Dean’s Office of the case. If the Deans can mediate, no further action is required. Otherwise, the Registrar's Office will organize a panel review with the Dean’s Office for an independent evaluation of the situation. The grade determined after this evaluation shall be the final grade.  

<details>  
<summary>References</summary>  

[Source: Academic-Policy_V5.1.pdf, Page: 10]
APPEALS: A student who wishes to dispute a final grade in a course should first discuss the matter with the course instructor(s). If the matter remains unresolved and the student believes there has been an error in grading, bias, or failure to follow published grading policies, the student may file an appeal as follows: • Submit the Review of Final Grade Request form to the Registrar's Office within five (05) business days from the date on which the Registrar's Office posts the final grade for the term. • The Registrar's Office informs the Dean’s Office of the case. After investigation, if the Deans can mediate, no further action is required. Otherwise, the Registrar's Office organizes a panel review with the Dean’s Office for an independent evaluation of the grade. The grade determined after this evaluation shall be the final grade. In cases concerning the interpretation of a course policy, the Dean’s Office will defer to the course syllabus whenever possible and otherwise will make a final ruling on the

[Source: Academic-Policy_V5.1.pdf, Page: 11]
as specified. 6.2 Academic Warning This is usually the first level of intervention for students who are not making satisfactory progress toward their degree and/or who fall below a 2.0 GPA, or for other reasons such as failure of attendance, participation, citizenship, or academic integrity. An Academic Warning is sent out by the Registrar’s Office. The student is required to attend an Academic Progress Meeting during which a Learning Contract will be created with specific conditions tailored to the individual situation. The Registrar's Office will be informed as a matter of record and follow-up. Three official warnings shall result in Disciplinary Action, constituting Academic Probation or Academic Suspension. 6.3 Academic Probation This is the second level of intervention. It is intended to make students aware that their academic performance puts them at risk of losing the opportunity to study at Fulbright, either temporarily (Suspension) or permanently (Dismissal). ### Question 98: I'm a third year student and don't know if I should do a capstone project then where should I go to get advice?  
### Answer: 

You should discuss with IS faculty prior to submitting the capstone proposal. This is important to ensure that your project idea is feasible, original, and aligns with the guidelines for the capstone project. The History Capstone Handbook also provides useful information for students wishing to pursue a capstone project. Additionally, you may want to consider proposing a Capstone project based on a 300-level research seminar that you have taken at Fulbright, or to ask the faculty for topic suggestions to increase your chances of finding a primary advisor who is also a subject-matter expert.

Allocation of advisor process As part of the application process, applicants will provide a first choice of primary and secondary advisor. It is not mandatory to have a secondary advisor. After the applications are

[Source: History Capstone Handbook - 2025-26.pdf, Page: 9]
The Capstone project is a year-long undertaking with less structure than a traditional course. It is certainly not the easiest way to complete your degree, and it may not be the most logical option for you, depending on your interests and your post-graduation plans. You should not consider it to be the default pathway to finishing your degree. One of the best reasons to undertake a Capstone project is if you enjoy doing historical research (which you will have sampled in Hands-On History and the research seminars you have completed) and want an opportunity to carry out a long-term research project. For such students, the Capstone year provides time and guidance that is unparalleled by any course or other opportunity at the undergraduate level. However, if you wish to graduate with distinction—an honorable goal— but you don’t particularly enjoy doing independent research, you may want to skip the Capstone and focus on GPA honors instead! Normally, the Capstone sequence begins in the Fall with Capstone I and

[Source: History Capstone Handbook - 2025-26.pdf, Page: 9]
requesting an external secondary advisor who does. Another way to approach this is to propose a Capstone project based on a 300-level research seminar that you have taken at Fulbright, or to ask the faculty for topic suggestions—that way, you are more likely to end up with a primary advisor who is also a subject-matter expert! The History Capstone Handbook, AY2025-26 student wishing to pursue journalism may want to complete their project in the form of a film or podcast. In general, although there can be exceptions, both thesis and non-thesis Capstones should ‘work up’ sources that do not figure extensively in existing scholarship, rather than taking the form of a literature review or commentary on existing secondary sources. This is something to discuss with a potential advisor. Guidelines for the Capstone by Thesis are included in Section 3 of this handbook. If students propose a project in an alternative format, the History faculty will confer and establish guidelines for the new format. 1.7. Group

### Question 99: I'm a member of Fulbright Basketball Club and going to attend a tournament. I need the official transcript and asking for some absence in classes then where should I get help?

To attend the tournament, you should first request an Excused Absence for the classes you will miss due to the university-sponsored event. The faculty or staff responsible for the basketball club should request a University Official Activity Excused Absence Request Form and submit it to the Dean’s Office, keeping Academic Affairs and Registrar’s Office in cc-ed for the record. You are responsible for submitting appropriate documentation and contacting your instructors to initiate arrangements to make up any missed work. After the tournament, you should write a reflection paper about your experience and submit it to ug.academic.affairs@fulbright.edu.vn no later than 7 days after you are back. As for the official transcript, you should contact the Registrar’s Office during business hours for assistance.

EXCEPTIONAL CIRCUMSTANCES: The University acknowledges that sometimes a student will experience circumstances that will impact their ability to fulfill the expectations of the University, including but not limited to assessment, attendance, and paying fees. Circumstances that may fall into this category are: • Exceptional medical circumstances, e.g., hospitalization or incapacitation through injury, illness, or mental health crisis. • Close bereavement, e.g., partner, child, parent, sibling, grandparent, and grandchild. Housemates or very close friends may also be considered as ‘close’, though evidence of the relationship may be required. • Victim of a serious crime • Disabilities for which reasonable adjustments are not yet in place and where the delay is not due to the student • Exceptional and unforeseeable transport difficulties e.g., major transport incidents, cancelled flights. This does not include everyday issues, e.g., traffic congestion, missed buses or trains. • Legal proceedings requiring

[Source: Academic-Policy_V5.1.pdf, Page: 7]
STUDENT ENROLLMENT: 3.1 Course Load and Credit Hours Fulbright University Vietnam uses the “credit hour” as the quantum for course workload in the undergraduate program. A credit hour typically represents 3 hours of work during each week of a 16-week term. For a 4- credit hour course, a student would, therefore, be expected to put in 12 hours of work per week, including class time, for a total of 192 hours of work during a term. There are earned credits and attempted credits. Earned credits refer to the number of credit hours a student successfully completes with a grade of D or higher for letter grade options and a Pass for Pass/No Pass options. Attempted credits are the credit hours students enroll in and are recorded in the transcript, regardless of whether they complete the courses or pass them. This includes all courses for which a student receives a grade, including withdrawals (W), incompletes (I), repeats (RP), and failures (F). See section 4 for more details on different types of grades. To graduate  

</details> 

### Question 101: How can I borrow books from the library?  
### Answer: 

To borrow books from the library, you would typically need to have a library card. If you are a student at Fulbright, you can apply for a library card. Once you have a library card, you can search for the books you need in the library's catalog, select the books you want to borrow, and then check them out at the circulation desk. Make sure to return the books by the due date to avoid fines. If the books you need are not available at your local library, you can request them through interlibrary loan.

### Question 102: How to work with major report?  
### Answer: 

To work with the major report for the Capstone by Applied and Creative Project, students should follow these steps:

1. Define clear objectives for the project.
2. Conduct a thorough literature review to understand the context and prior work.
3. Develop a detailed project plan and timeline for Capstone 2.
4. Submit the report on Canvas by the deadline.
5. The report should include at least the following sections:
   - Introduction/Motivation for the problem
   - Literature review
   - Problem statement/description
   - Proposed methods, plan, and timeline for Capstone 2
6. The report should be a production book with writing about what students have researched, observed, experienced, solved, and lessons learned. It should include all pre-production deliverables and production documents.
7. The word count (not including production documents) should be under 5000 words. The format can follow the thesis style guidelines.
8. The report should include the intellectual rationale of the project, the goals of the project, evaluation questions, a critical evaluation, and documentation of the process.
9. The evaluation report is scored based on the completeness, critical depth, intellectual rigor, and effective use of evidence and theory, not on whether the project appears to have met its goals.
10. If the project involves a non-academic advisor, students should request their involvement in consultation with and subject to the approval of their primary and secondary academic advisors from the SOCI major.

### Question 103: How many way can I fill in the requirements of EL?  
### Answer: 

You can fulfill the Experiential Learning (EL) requirements in the following ways:

1. By completing at least 4 credits and a maximum of 12 credits under the Experiential Learning Program (ELP) as a graduation requirement.

2. If your advisor approves, EL can also count toward elective or major requirements.

3. If you choose to do a capstone project, you can fulfill 8 credits of your major requirements via a capstone project. However, this is optional and you can choose to fulfill 8 credits of coursework as specified in your major if you don't do a capstone.

4. If you have interdisciplinary minors, the requirements mainly consist of courses from other majors. These courses are usually not cross-listed with the minors and are referred to as 'tagged' by these minors. These tagged courses can also contribute to your EL requirements, again upon advisor approval.

5. Electives can also contribute to your EL requirements if they are experiential learning experiences, again upon advisor approval.

6. You can also use electives to fulfill requirements for another minor or major, which could indirectly contribute to your EL requirements.

Fulbright’s Experiential Learning Program (ELP) exists to create, standardize, and facilitate academic credit-bearing experiential learning experiences. All full-time, undergraduate, degree- seeking students must complete at least 04 credits and a maximum of 12 credits under the ELP as a graduation requirement. Current ELP streams are housed within Academic Affairs (AA), Career Services (CS), and Center for Entrepreneurship and Innovation (CEI), where each team is responsible for administrative and academic duties of their respective stream(s). The ELP operates within Fulbright’s undergraduate program’s standard operating procedures and is developed in consultation with undergraduate program leadership and faculty. For more details, please refer here https://onestop.fulbright.edu.vn/s/article/Experiential-Learning- Program 13.5  Electives To complete the degree, students are free to take elective courses from the Course Catalogue.
